 [![Qui-Gon Jinn was given a Jedi funeral on Naboo, memorializing the Jedi Master.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/FuneralOfQuiGonJinn-TPM.png/revision/latest?cb=20130118050103) [![Qui-Gon Jinn was given a Jedi funeral on Naboo, memorializing the Jedi Master.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/FuneralOfQuiGonJinn-TPM.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130118050103)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/FuneralOfQuiGonJinn-TPM.png/revision/latest?cb=20130118050103) 

Qui-Gon Jinn was given a Jedi funeral on Naboo, memorializing the Jedi Master.

 

In the aftermath of the battle, in which the Naboo successfully captured the Viceroy and ended the Federation occupation, Kenobi was granted the Jedi Knight rank and insisted on taking Skywalker as his apprentice. Although Yoda disagreed, the Council approved Kenobi's request, fulfilling Jinn's dying wish: Skywalker would undergo Jedi training. Later,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Jinn was memorialized[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36) when he was given a Jedi [funeral](/wiki/Funeral_of_Qui-Gon_Jinn "Funeral of Qui-Gon Jinn") on Naboo, where his body was [cremated](/wiki/Cremation "Cremation") on a [funeral](/wiki/Funeral "Funeral") pyre. Many delegates, including Queen Amidala, the Jedi Council, and Chancellor Palpatine, attended the funeral;[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) notably absent were his former master Dooku and Jedi Master [Yaddle](/wiki/Yaddle "Yaddle"), who, suspicious of Dooku's intended absence, followed Dooku in his confrontation with Darth Sidious in [Coruscant](/wiki/Coruscant "Coruscant").[[3]](#cite_note-The_Sith_Lord-3) At the funeral, Kenobi told Skywalker that the Council would allow him to be trained and that Kenobi would be his master. Together, the two mourned the death of their fallen friend, as Kenobi vowed that Skywalker would become a Jedi.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Amongst the Jedi, Jinn was remembered as a great member of their Order[[24]](#cite_note-AoR_Dooku-24) despite his past of disagreeing with the council.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

Even though he had always wanted Jinn available as guidance for when he eventually trained a Padawan,[[20]](#cite_note-AoR_Obi-Wan-20) and he had wanted time between his apprenticeship and eventual mentorship to decide what kind of Jedi he should be without Jinn by his side,[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) Kenobi upheld his vow to his master dutifully over the years. At one point, when Skywalker was considering leaving the Jedi Order [at the age of twelve](/wiki/29_BBY "29 BBY"), Kenobi was intent on following suit. However, he was still going to complete the boy's training even outside the Order. Skywalker, however, chose to remain a Jedi in the aftermath of a [mission](/wiki/Mission_to_Carnelion_IV "Mission to Carnelion IV") to the planet [Carnelion IV](/wiki/Carnelion_IV "Carnelion IV").[[40]](#cite_note-OW_&_A-40) Even though Kenobi could become easily annoyed by Skywalker—leaving him to question if he had ever annoyed Jinn in similar ways, although he doubted he ever had—he nevertheless befriended[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) and grew close to his Padawan, with the Jedi duo coming to act like brothers.[[41]](#cite_note-Obi-Wan_&_Anakin-41)

Although Skywalker remained thankful of Kenobi's teachings, he, at times, pondered how his life as a Jedi would have changed if Jinn had survived; even though he knew the Jedi Order disapproved of attachments, he thought these questions were alright because he believed nothing—not even interpersonal relationships—could ever be fully untethered.[[42]](#cite_note-Ahsoka-42) As Kenobi later recognized, Skywalker developed a habit of growing very connected to and not wanting to lose anyone he was close with after leaving his mother. Desperate for new connections, he had found one with Jinn, only for the Jedi Master to be taken away from him[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) shortly after they met.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

Dooku, still a Sith in secret, eventually learned of Jinn's death at the hands of Maul. Later, on the planet [Sullust](/wiki/Sullust "Sullust"), Dooku unexpectedly reunited with the Jedi Knight Jak'zin, who noted he had met Jinn before being interrupted by a representative of the [SoroSuub Corporation](/wiki/SoroSuub_Corporation "SoroSuub Corporation"). Later, Dooku, appearing as if he could be compassionate ally, discussed Jinn with the Jedi Knight. Dooku claimed he wondered if his former apprentice would still be alive if he had not left the order, reflecting that the company of Kenobi was not enough to save the late master. The Sith used his speculations to trick Jak'zin into letting him in on the Jedi's [mission on Sullust](/wiki/Mission_on_Sullust "Mission on Sullust").[[24]](#cite_note-AoR_Dooku-24)

##### Effect on Naboo[]

:   "*His name was Qui-Gon Jinn, a Jedi. He died defending Naboo during the battle for the planet against the Trade Federation. The Jedi memorialized him there, and we honor him as a hero.*"
:   ―Padmé Amidala, to Bail Organa[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

Amidala, meanwhile, came to believe that her relationship with Jinn had been an odd one, given that he had seen through her disguise, yet she hoped she would have been able to consider him a friend and ally if he had survived. In the years following the Naboo Crisis, she remained saddened by his death, and she made sure to light a candle of incense for the fallen Jedi during the yearly memorial for all who had died for Naboo. In fact, many others did the same; though few on Naboo had met the Jedi Master, it was believed everyone on the world knew his name, with Naboo like [Tonra](/wiki/Tonra "Tonra")—who had actually been present for many of the so-called "stories" about what had happened—hearing tales of what he did for their planet. For years after the invasion, the handmaiden [Saché](/wiki/Sach%C3%A9 "Saché") continued to incorrectly believe Jinn had been fooled by the decoy act[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36) like most had been.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

 [![Honoring him as a hero, Padmé Amidala remained saddened over Jinn's death, hoping that they could have been true friends.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/AgeofRepublic-PadmeCoverArt.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20181219055938) [![Honoring him as a hero, Padmé Amidala remained saddened over Jinn's death, hoping that they could have been true friends.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/AgeofRepublic-PadmeCoverArt.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/190?cb=20181219055938)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/AgeofRepublic-PadmeCoverArt.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20181219055938) 

Honoring him as a hero, Padmé Amidala remained saddened over Jinn's death, hoping that they could have been true friends.

 

Nevertheless, events like Jinn's time on Tatooine were not part of public record, so they were not spread amongst the Naboo. However, Tonra and Sabé discussed such events during a mission to the desert world. Ultimately, the people of Naboo honored Jinn as a hero who had given everything to save them.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36) One of the ways they honored him was by building a shrine to his memory, a [shrine](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn_shrine "Qui-Gon Jinn shrine") which was known to gain some popularity over the next ten years and was visited by Anakin Skywalker shortly before his [secret wedding](/wiki/Wedding_of_Anakin_Skywalker_and_Padm%C3%A9_Amidala "Wedding of Anakin Skywalker and Padmé Amidala") to Padmé Amidala.[[43]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-43) Several years after the invasion, when Amidala was asked if she would become Naboo's Galactic Senator after her term as queen ended, she looked to the Handmaiden [Saché](/wiki/Sach%C3%A9 "Saché"); the Handmaiden remembered when Jinn asked them to go to Coruscant, given that Amidala had have to give a similar wordless signal to her allies.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

Having met Jedi, Amidala was unique amongst her colleagues in the Senate, but she nevertheless found the manners of the Jedi Order unsettling. She considered that her reaction to their ways may have ended up different if Jinn had survived. While speaking with Senator [Bail Prestor Organa](/wiki/Bail_Prestor_Organa "Bail Prestor Organa") after he too had realized Amidala used decoys, albeit only after seeing Padmé in a guard's uniform while Sabé was acting as the Senator at a gala, she told him about Jinn, feeling a great sadness wash over herself while she explained his fate. Organa responded that he was sorry for her loss, further stating that he realized Jinn's death was an example of the dangerous life that followed her. Having been told Jinn was the only other person who had managed to deduce she used decoys in the midst of the maneuver, Organa admitted he was happy to have found himself in what he deemed to be excellent company.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

For a mission to the planet [Bromlarch](/wiki/Bromlarch "Bromlarch"), Amidala and several other senators partnered with Jedi Master Depa Billaba, whom the former queen recognized due to her being present at Jinn's funeral. While she found it odd to interact with a Jedi Knight once more, Amidala also noticed Billaba carried herself very differently from how Jinn had. While she understood all Jedi in their Order would be different, she could not let go of the strange feeling it gave her, as if Billaba looked through her, while Jinn had taken the time to look at her. Soon afterward, Amidala met the liaison [Ninui](/wiki/Ninui "Ninui"); given that it was the first time the liaison was meeting a Jedi, Amidala noted how she had met Kenobi and Jinn, explaining that the Jedi were people like them, albeit people whose teachings could be confusing to non-Force-sensitives, and Ninui noted she wished to hear the complete story of how she met them.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

#### Surviving as a spirit[]

:   "*Anakin! Anakin! NO!*"
:   ―Qui-Gon Jinn trying to hold Anakin back through the Force as he massacres the Tuskens[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12)

Though his training had been incomplete, Jinn utilized what he learned from the Force Priestesses to become one with the Force and retain his identity after his death. However, he hadn't fully learned the mystery, so he could not physically manifest himself, only speak as a disembodied voice.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

 [![When Anakin Skywalker prepared to murder Tusken Raiders, Jinn tried to stop him, but the young Chosen One ignored the Jedi Master's voice.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/Anakin_Vengeance.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070315204029) [![When Anakin Skywalker prepared to murder Tusken Raiders, Jinn tried to stop him, but the young Chosen One ignored the Jedi Master's voice.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/Anakin_Vengeance.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/190?cb=20070315204029)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/Anakin_Vengeance.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070315204029) 

When Anakin Skywalker prepared to murder Tusken Raiders, Jinn tried to stop him, but the young Chosen One ignored the Jedi Master's voice.

 

One time that Jinn communicated through the Force was approximately ten years after the events on Naboo. Skywalker had [returned](/wiki/Mission_to_rescue_Shmi_Skywalker_Lars "Mission to rescue Shmi Skywalker Lars") to Tatooine to find his mother, about whom he had been having recurring nightmares, and discovered she had been kidnapped by [Tusken Raiders](/wiki/Tusken_Raider "Tusken Raider"). He found her in a [Tusken camp](/wiki/Unidentified_Tusken_village "Unidentified Tusken village"), but she died only moments later. In his anger, Skywalker slaughtered all the Tuskens in the camp. Feeling the great pain and distress, Jinn called out to Skywalker through the Force, which Yoda could hear—but not comprehend—through his own [meditations](/wiki/Meditation "Meditation"). In Jinn's own words, he begged Anakin to listen to his better nature and refuse to give in to his hatred.[[43]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-43) However, Jinn's pleas were for naught, as Skywalker didn't heed his words in his uncontrolled rage,[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) telling himself that he was only imagining Jinn's presence in that moment.[[43]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-43)

In the meantime, Dooku, who had remained a Sith and became the [Head of State](/wiki/Head_of_State "Head of State") of the [Confederacy of Independent Systems](/wiki/Confederacy_of_Independent_Systems "Confederacy of Independent Systems"), captured Kenobi on the planet [Geonosis](/wiki/Geonosis "Geonosis"). While interrogating Kenobi, Dooku—who was also secretly a Sith Lord—expressed his belief that Jinn would have joined his cause if he had been alive. Shortly after that, a conflict known as the Clone Wars began between the Galactic Republic and Dooku's Confederacy.[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) Shortly after the conflict's beginning, Skywalker prepared himself to partake in a [secret wedding with Senator Amidala](/wiki/Wedding_of_Anakin_Skywalker_and_Padm%C3%A9_Amidala "Wedding of Anakin Skywalker and Padmé Amidala"). As part of his preparation, he visited [Jinn's shrine](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn_shrine "Qui-Gon Jinn shrine") on Naboo in partial repentance for having refused to heed Jinn's words during his rage against the sand people, additionally having realized it meant there was a chance his old mentor could somehow see him and offer advice. Although he had told himself he had only imagined Jinn's presence, he knew he was lying to himself. While at the shrine, Skywalker attempted to reach out to the Force in an attempt to connect with Jinn in a similar manner to that previous instance. The attempt seemingly yielded nothing in his senses, which he theorized was Jinn's way of telling him that things could always be made right.[[43]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-43)

After feeling a sudden sense of calm despite the brewing Clone Wars, he then expressed his thanks despite not knowing if Qui-Gon was responsible for his personal interpretations.[[43]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-43) During the Clone Wars, Skywalker was promoted to the rank of Jedi Knight and was assigned a Padawan of his own, the Togruta [Ahsoka Tano](/wiki/Ahsoka_Tano "Ahsoka Tano"), to whom he recited Jinn's teachings on at least one occasion.[[44]](#cite_note-TCW_film-44) Additionally, Jinn's teachings were indirectly passed down to Tano during her apprenticeship, as she was learning from Skywalker, who had learned from Kenobi, who had learned from Jinn.[[45]](#cite_note-Together_Again_Download-45) Despite the fact that he was dead,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) the Confederacy put out a citizen's alert on Jinn and offered a 50,000 credit reward, charging him with conspiracy against the Trade Federation.[[46]](#cite_note-Jedi_Hunt_Qui-Gon-46)

The Jedi made an effort to capture Dooku during the war, feeling his arrest could help bring an end to the fighting.[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) During one attempt to capture him[[47]](#cite_note-Dooku_Captured_story-47) in [21 BBY](/wiki/21_BBY "21 BBY"),[[48]](#cite_note-21_BBY_Date-48) Skywalker and Kenobi boarded the count's [*Munificent*-class star frigate](/wiki/Count_Dooku%27s_frigate "Count Dooku's frigate"), yet the Sith Lord managed to escape through a secret hatch. Skywalker pursued, making Dooku shoot Force lightning at the Jedi Knight; according to what Dooku said in a recording he intended to send to Darth Sidious, he knew such an attack would not defeat Skywalker, believing that—because his Padawan Jinn had trained Kenobi, who had trained Skywalker—his personal power had partly been passed down to his foe. He only intended to block the Jedi's sight to enable his escape. Later in the same recording, Dooku—recalling how he, Skywalker, and Kenobi had been captured by the [Ohnaka Gang](/wiki/Ohnaka_Gang "Ohnaka Gang") of [pirates](/wiki/Pirate "Pirate")—again mentioned Jinn, feeling that Skywalker was a fool who did not compare to the apprentices he had trained. Ultimately, Dooku did not send the message to Sidious.[[47]](#cite_note-Dooku_Captured_story-47)

 [![Jinn's appearance to Kenobi on Mortis.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/63/QuiGonJinnCW.png/revision/latest?cb=20130524220028) [![Jinn's appearance to Kenobi on Mortis.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/63/QuiGonJinnCW.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130524220028)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/63/QuiGonJinnCW.png/revision/latest?cb=20130524220028) 

Jinn's appearance to Kenobi on Mortis.

 

Due to his incomplete training, Jinn's spirit couldn't physically manifest himself, but he occurred in a vision on one known occasion;[[49]](#cite_note-Databank_Gallery-49) Kenobi, Skywalker, and Tano, had been [lured](/wiki/Mission_to_Mortis "Mission to Mortis") to the planet [Mortis](/wiki/Mortis "Mortis") by [three beings](/wiki/Force_wielder "Force wielder") known as the [Father](/wiki/Father_(Mortis) "Father (Mortis)"), [Son](/wiki/Son "Son"), and [Daughter](/wiki/Daughter "Daughter"). These beings believed that Skywalker was the Chosen One, as did Jinn, whose vision first appeared to Kenobi to warn him that the beings sought Skywalker and his potential as the Chosen One, to use it for their own means. When Kenobi questioned how Jinn could appear, the figure told him that the planet acted as an amplifier and that it was a conduit through which the Force flowed. The two spoke about Skywalker and his power, with Kenobi having the opportunity to tell Jinn that the late Jedi Master's predictions about Skywalker were true: he was stronger than any other Jedi, yet still could not find balance. Jinn warned that if Skywalker were the Chosen One, then the boy would discover it on Mortis. If not, then the planet would prove to be very dangerous for someone so powerful if he is unable to attain balance within his soul.[[50]](#cite_note-Overlords-50)

Skywalker himself later experienced Jinn's vision. The figure of the late Jedi informed him that he still believed the boy would bring balance to the Force after facing his [demons](/wiki/Demon "Demon"). After the three Jedi escaped Mortis, where the Father professed his belief that Skywalker was the Chosen One,[[51]](#cite_note-GhostsMortis-51) Although it had truly been Jinn who appeared before them,[[52]](#cite_note-CVD-52) Kenobi came to believe, and told the Jedi Council, that the appearance of his old mentor was simply an illusion, one manifested from their memories by the beings on Mortis; however, Skywalker wasn't as confident, despite Jedi teachings saying that it was impossible for a being to retain their identity after death. The report about Mortis did not change these Jedi beliefs or teachings.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

#### Guiding Yoda[]

:   "*It is I, Qui-Gon Jinn.*"  
    "*That cannot be. Dead, you are.*"  
    "*No. I am part of the Living Force, Yoda.*"
:   ―Jinn communes to Yoda during the Clone Wars[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

The Clone Wars also saw the return of Jinn's murderer, Darth Maul. Believed to have been killed by Kenobi on Naboo, Maul had survived, replacing his lower body with a cybernetic apparatus.[[53]](#cite_note-Brothers-53) Maul sought revenge on Kenobi for maiming him, and the two fought on several occasions;[[54]](#cite_note-Revenge-54)[[55]](#cite_note-Revival-55)[[56]](#cite_note-The_Lawless-56) prior to the [first of these duels](/wiki/Skirmish_above_Raydonia "Skirmish above Raydonia"), Maul recalled how he had killed Jinn before being cut down himself, proving to Kenobi that his old foe had indeed returned. During the duel itself, he mocked Kenobi by recalling how he had murdered Jinn, making the Jedi Master briefly give into anger to strike against his mentor's murderer.[[54]](#cite_note-Revenge-54) Although Maul was captured during the [Siege of Mandalore](/wiki/Siege_of_Mandalore "Siege of Mandalore"), which occurred during the waning days of the Clone Wars,[[57]](#cite_note-The_Phantom_Apprentice-57) he escaped and survived the conflict.[[58]](#cite_note-Victory_and_Death-58)

 [![During the waning days of the Clone Wars, Qui-Gon Jinn reached out to Yoda.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/91/YodaHearsQui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20140713170416) [![During the waning days of the Clone Wars, Qui-Gon Jinn reached out to Yoda.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/91/YodaHearsQui-Gon.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20140713170416)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/91/YodaHearsQui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20140713170416) 

During the waning days of the Clone Wars, Qui-Gon Jinn reached out to Yoda.

 

It was not until the Clone Wars' waning days that Yoda learned Jinn had retained his consciousness after death. Knowing Yoda was destined to be a significant player in bringing balance to the Force, and that it was Yoda's destiny to complete the training Jinn himself did not, the late Jedi Master spoke to Yoda through the Force. He guided him to [Dagobah](/wiki/Dagobah "Dagobah"), the first leg on Yoda's trials, to determine whether he was ready to learn the secrets. Jinn told Yoda about his training and how the Living Force fed into the Cosmic Force, allowing him to return after death. At first, Yoda was only interested in the Clone Wars' truth, asking if he knew the identity of Darth Sidious, but Jinn could only guide Yoda through his trials. The Living Force guided Yoda in the form of a glowing swarm of [fireflies](/wiki/Firefly "Firefly"). Later they directed Yoda to the planet of the Force Priestesses, where Yoda could continue his trial.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

Yoda completed the trials and was deemed worthy of learning the secret of eternal consciousness,[[13]](#cite_note-Sacrifice-13) as Yoda would one day train the [person](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker") who would help Skywalker bring balance to the Force.[[59]](#cite_note-Destiny-59) The Force Priestesses instructed that Jinn would guide Yoda's training.[[13]](#cite_note-Sacrifice-13) After the end of the Clone Wars and the [fall](/wiki/Order_66 "Order 66") of the Jedi Order, Yoda chose to go into exile on Dagobah, but not before telling Kenobi that Jinn had returned from the [netherworld of the Force](/wiki/Netherworld_of_the_Force "Netherworld of the Force") and could guide his former Padawan in learning the secret.[[60]](#cite_note-Episode_III-60) However, Obi-Wan was unable to make contact with Qui-Gon until[[38]](#cite_note-Skywalker:_AFaW-38) [9 BBY](/wiki/9_BBY "9 BBY")[[61]](#cite_note-Kenobi_Date-61) despite sometimes hearing him as a voice in his head.[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) One time during meditation, he felt himself phase out of reality for a few moments. During this time, he felt Jinn commune through the Force with him, with his old Jedi Master telling him to let go.[[42]](#cite_note-Ahsoka-42)

#### Guiding Obi-Wan Kenobi[]

:   "*Master Qui-Gon."*  
    "*Well, took you long enough.*"  
    "*Beginning to think you'd never come.*"  
    "*I was always here, Obi-Wan. You were just not ready to see. Come on. We've got a ways to go.*"
:   ―Obi-Wan Kenobi and Qui-Gon reuniting[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63)

 [![Jinn's lightsaber (bottom right) was taken with Kenobi while he was in exile.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/ForceCollection-Ben-Kenobi.png/revision/latest?cb=20230326153514) [![Jinn's lightsaber (bottom right) was taken with Kenobi while he was in exile.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/ForceCollection-Ben-Kenobi.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/236?cb=20230326153514)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/06/ForceCollection-Ben-Kenobi.png/revision/latest?cb=20230326153514) 

Jinn's lightsaber (bottom right) was taken with Kenobi while he was in exile.

 

The end of the Clone Wars also saw the fall of Anakin Skywalker, who was seduced to the dark side of the Force by Sidious, becoming the Sith Lord [Darth](/wiki/Darth "Darth") Vader.[[60]](#cite_note-Episode_III-60) The fall confirmed the Council's fears about Skywalker's training,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) but he was still the Chosen One.[[64]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-64) During Obi-Wan Kenobi's self-imposed exile on Tatooine, where he watched over Anakin's son, Luke Skywalker, he frequently dwelled upon his failure to train Skywalker. At one point, he traveled to Shmi Skywalker's grave and apologized for failing to complete Jinn's promise.[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) Kenobi also had possession of his master's lightsaber during his exile.[[65]](#cite_note-Jedi_in_Hiding-65)

Shortly following Anakin's fall to the dark side, Qui-Gon started to push himself to emerge fully in the land of the living[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) instead of remaining a voice.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) Qui-Gon committed to the effort to ensure that Obi-Wan did not have to spend his following years on Tatooine alone. Overall, it took Qui-Gon nearly a decade before his efforts finally met success.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) While it was sometime before Kenobi saw his former master again,[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63) he often spoke to Jinn[[67]](#cite_note-Part_I-67) but began to fear his master would never appear. In reality, Jinn was always with Kenobi, even if Kenobi was not emotionally ready to see him due to his guilt over Skywalker's fall.[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63)

One morning[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) in [16 BBY](/wiki/16_BBY "16 BBY"),[[68]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death_flashback_date-68) when Skywalker was three, Jinn spoke to Kenobi after he awoke from a nightmare, warning him to get to the boy to protect him. Thus, Kenobi raced to the [Lars Homestead](/wiki/Lars_homestead "Lars homestead"), where Luke was being raised by his aunt and uncle, [Beru](/wiki/Beru_Whitesun_Lars "Beru Whitesun Lars") and [Owen Lars](/wiki/Owen_Lars "Owen Lars"). Once there, Kenobi helped defend against a gang of bandits, yet Owen demanded he never return after the skirmish.[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62)

| This section of the article assumes 100% game completion of *[Star Wars Jedi: Survivor](/wiki/Star_Wars_Jedi:_Survivor "Star Wars Jedi: Survivor")*. Any alternate stories may be noted in the "[Behind the scenes](#Behind_the_scenes)" section. The events in this section may or may not have been confirmed as [canon](/wiki/Canon "Canon"). |
| --- |

In 9 BBY,[[69]](#cite_note-SurvivorDate-69) Jedi Master Eno Cordova recounted his friendship and introduction to Jinn to Jedi Knight [Cal Kestis](/wiki/Cal_Kestis "Cal Kestis").[[15]](#cite_note-JediSurvivor-15)

Assumption ends here.

 [![Jinn appears to Kenobi for the first time as a Force spirit.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/29/JinnAppearsToKenobi-OWKpVI.png/revision/latest?cb=20220723192410) [![Jinn appears to Kenobi for the first time as a Force spirit.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/29/JinnAppearsToKenobi-OWKpVI.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20220723192410)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/29/JinnAppearsToKenobi-OWKpVI.png/revision/latest?cb=20220723192410) 

Jinn appears to Kenobi for the first time as a Force spirit.

 

In 9 BBY,[[70]](#cite_note-Kenobi_VI_date-70) after Kenobi had another [duel](/wiki/Fight_on_a_barren_moon "Fight on a barren moon") with Vader and came to terms with Skywalker's fall, Qui-Gon appeared to Obi-Wan as the latter was riding towards [Beggar's Canyon](/wiki/Beggar%27s_Canyon "Beggar's Canyon"), telling his former Padawan that it had taken him long enough. Obi-Wan showed amazement at his appearance, stating that he had begun to think that Qui-Gon would never arrive. Qui-Gon then clarified that he had always been there, and that Obi-Wan had not been ready to see him prior to that moment. Qui-Gon then asked for Obi-Wan to continue following him, with Qui-Gon disappearing from view as he proceeded further into the canyon, Obi-Wan following shortly.[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63) In the years after the Clone Wars, Kenobi and Yoda completed their training to retain their consciousness after death.[[71]](#cite_note-Episode_V-71)[[64]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-64) During his time on Tatooine, Kenobi continued to speak with Jinn, telling him about the hardships of living in exile and Skywalker's possible destiny of the Chosen One.[[72]](#cite_note-Journals_7-72)[[73]](#cite_note-Journals-73)

After Anakin's fall to the dark side, Jinn continued his training to manifest himself, becoming clearer to Kenobi over the course of his visits to him. The two never discussed Jinn's supposed mistakes whenever he traveled into the mortal universe; Kenobi did not blame his old master for Skywalker's fall, while Jinn thought his old Padawan did.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) During an encounter with the [Wookiee](/wiki/Wookiee "Wookiee") bounty hunter [Krrsantan](/wiki/Krrsantan "Krrsantan"), Kenobi called upon his Master to give him strength to defeat the foe.[[74]](#cite_note-Journals_20-74) Kenobi finally killed a resurgent Maul in a [duel](/wiki/Mission_to_Tatooine_(Imperial_Era) "Mission to Tatooine (Imperial Era)") on Tatooine in [2 BBY](/wiki/2_BBY "2 BBY"),[[75]](#cite_note-Twin_Suns_date-75) using Jinn's [Ataru](/wiki/Form_IV "Form IV") stance to defend himself against Maul.[[76]](#cite_note-Twin_Suns-76) In [1 BBY](/wiki/1_BBY "1 BBY"),[[77]](#cite_note-Chronology_Note-77) Jinn's voice was heard by Padawan [Ezra Bridger](/wiki/Ezra_Bridger "Ezra Bridger") during his mission to a [place](/wiki/World_Between_Worlds "World Between Worlds") that existed between time and [space](/wiki/Realspace "Realspace").[[78]](#cite_note-A_World_Between_Worlds-78)

After Kenobi introduced Skywalker to the life of a Jedi, as the droids R2-D2 and C-3PO had arrived on Tatooine with [secret plans](/wiki/Death_Star_plans "Death Star plans") that needed to be delivered to the [Rebel Alliance](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic"), Skywalker rushed off to the Lars Homestead, having realized the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire")'s [stormtroopers](/wiki/Stormtrooper "Stormtrooper") would track the droids to his aunt and uncle.[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79) Jinn was compelled to appear after hearing Kenobi call his name, taking on the exact same appearance that he had carried in life and appearing a few [centimeters](/wiki/Centimeter "Centimeter") from his former Padawan. Kenobi asked for his guidance, as he feared that the Empire would capture Luke upon his return to the Lars Homestead. Already knowing the circumstances Kenobi was speaking of, Jinn informed him that he had seen Luke's destiny go beyond the current event, listing off possible solutions that would occur, while the surrounding landscape became clearer to him. He spotted the corpses of [Jawas](/wiki/Jawa "Jawa"), feeling the memory of their deaths wash over him, but was slightly comforted when he noticed R2-D2 and C-3PO; he believed it was the work of the Force, bringing them back to where Anakin's journey had begun.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

 [![When Luke Skywalker rushed off to save his uncle and aunt, Obi-Wan Kenobi called out to Jinn for guidance.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/Right-before-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20210831221547) [![When Luke Skywalker rushed off to save his uncle and aunt, Obi-Wan Kenobi called out to Jinn for guidance.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/Right-before-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20210831221547)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/Right-before-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20210831221547) 

When Luke Skywalker rushed off to save his uncle and aunt, Obi-Wan Kenobi called out to Jinn for guidance.

 

The news that Luke would survive relieved Kenobi, yet Jinn knew his former apprentice had no idea how the young man's journey would unfold. When Kenobi confided in him that he found it difficult to give up his exile, Jinn understood it was a symptom of him adapting to the new life, informing him that he would quickly feel like a Jedi Knight when the time came. He also congratulated his former student on remaining steadfast in his devotion to the light side. He also apologized to Kenobi, believing he had failed his Padawan long ago when he made him train Anakin. Kenobi disagreed, arguing that Anakin was the main person at fault for his fall, but Jinn resolved to wait to discuss this matter, knowing that the two of them would be together in the Force soon;[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) in the near future, Kenobi would [sacrifice](/wiki/Rescue_of_Princess_Leia "Rescue of Princess Leia") himself to save Luke and be struck down by Darth Vader,[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79) and Jinn knew this was coming.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Jinn and Kenobi then both felt Luke's horror at seeing his aunt and uncle, [Beru](/wiki/Beru_Whitesun_Lars "Beru Whitesun Lars") and Owen Lars, dead outside their home. Even so, Kenobi sensed Luke's reaction at a greater remove, while Jinn, due to him being of the Force, could see their burned corpses in front of him, as clearly as he could see Kenobi. Thinking his former Padawan needed guidance, he then told Kenobi that he had made the right choice in choosing not to tell Luke everything about Anakin; he knew Luke could have gone down his father's path if Kenobi had revealed everything, or he could have thought Owen was right about Kenobi being insane, which would have resulted in him being killed with his aunt and uncle. After telling Kenobi to wait to reveal the truth until Luke was ready, Jinn's appearance was very nearly corporeal, the clearest Kenobi had ever seen his master's spirit. Jinn illuminated him in some of the ways he had managed it, all the while, considering that Kenobi did not have long to live. Sensing that Luke would soon return, he bade farewell, telling Kenobi that they would meet again soon. His former student did not understand the true meaning of the statement, and Jinn disappeared, returning to the Force.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn knew that his former apprentice would fall to Darth Vader aboard the Death Star.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/Jotr-macewindu-2-40thvariant.png/revision/latest?cb=20190118021729) [![Qui-Gon Jinn knew that his former apprentice would fall to Darth Vader aboard the Death Star.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/Jotr-macewindu-2-40thvariant.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20190118021729)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/Jotr-macewindu-2-40thvariant.png/revision/latest?cb=20190118021729) 

Qui-Gon Jinn knew that his former apprentice would fall to Darth Vader aboard the Death Star.

 

On the [DS-1 Death Star Mobile Battle Station](/wiki/DS-1_Orbital_Battle_Station "DS-1 Orbital Battle Station"), Kenobi was indeed killed by Darth Vader to protect Luke.[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79) After his death, Kenobi found himself overwhelmed by visions of the past, present, and future; among the people he saw was Jinn, including when he was slain by Maul and when his voice told him to protect Luke[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) in 16 BBY.[[68]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death_flashback_date-68) While worried about not completing Luke's training as he lived through his past, relived the present, and saw glimpses of the future, Kenobi again heard that Luke had called out to him on the Death Star; hearing Jinn's voice, louder than it had been for years, telling him to go with Luke, Kenobi ensured his spirit would remain with the Jedi trainee. Thus,[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) after his death, Kenobi first appeared as a disembodied voice, telling Luke to flee the [Death Star](/wiki/DS-1_Orbital_Battle_Station "DS-1 Orbital Battle Station") with his friends, and then later to guide Luke through the [Battle of Yavin](/wiki/Battle_of_Yavin "Battle of Yavin"), helping the young Force-sensitive to destroy the Death Star.[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79)

Yoda, meanwhile, had hidden himself on Dagobah, staying away from the Empire, but also growing lonely over the years. Fortunately, he knew how to call out to Jinn for company. One of the few personal items Yoda brought with him was [Jinn's cloak](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn%27s_cloak "Qui-Gon Jinn's cloak"), which he made into his blanket. Around the time of Kenobi's death, Yoda was preparing to move to the lowlands of Dagobah for the dry season, and he found himself questioning how long ago Jinn had died when he counted his personal items for the journey. He also realized that, while people strong in the Force could sometimes leave an imprint of themselves in what they owned, too many years had gone by for any trace of the Jedi Master to remain in the cloak, if he had ever felt such a trace at all. As he always did, he gathered his cane, several seeds, a pot made by Kenobi, and Jinn's cloak before making his way down to his lowland hut.[[80]](#cite_note-There_is_Another-80)

As he journeyed, he felt Kenobi and Vader's duel in the Force, taking his focus away as an old Imperial [probe droid](/wiki/Probe_droid "Probe droid") finally located him. After throwing Kenobi's pot into the droid to destroy it, he sensed Kenobi's death, distracting him as two other probes appeared. One fired and hit Yoda's carrying bag, which he rushed to to protect Jinn's cloak from burning. After taking out the droids, he saw that the cloak was only slightly singed and that his seeds were fine. Afterward, Jinn, currently in the [netherworld of the Force](/wiki/Netherworld_of_the_Force "Netherworld of the Force"), laughed at Yoda, which the Jedi Master sensed. Once Yoda moved back into his lowland hut, he trimmed the cloak, which also meant it better compensated for his shrinking size. Several days after his move, Yoda, missing the friends he had lost, called out to Jinn to appear from the netherworld several times, only to be unable to sense him.[[80]](#cite_note-There_is_Another-80)

Jinn was in fact preoccupied, so Kenobi instead appeared. During his visit, Kenobi quipped that Yoda's encounter with the probe droids could not have been too dangerous, given that he had saved Jinn's cloak, annoying Yoda. Afterward, Kenobi asked him to train Luke, which Yoda reluctantly agreed to.[[80]](#cite_note-There_is_Another-80)

#### The lives and times of Luke and Rey[]

:   "*Every Jedi who ever lived lives in you. We stand behind you, Rey. Rise.*"
:   ―Qui-Gon speaks to Rey[[81]](#cite_note-Episode_9-81)

 [![Skywalker, Kenobi, and Yoda all learned the secret of eternal consciousness.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/JediGhosts-ROTJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20201008104501) [![Skywalker, Kenobi, and Yoda all learned the secret of eternal consciousness.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/JediGhosts-ROTJ.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20201008104501)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/55/JediGhosts-ROTJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20201008104501) 

Skywalker, Kenobi, and Yoda all learned the secret of eternal consciousness.

 

In the aftermath of the Battle of Yavin, Vader was [shot down](/wiki/Battle_of_Vrogas_Vas "Battle of Vrogas Vas") over the planet [Vrogas Vas](/wiki/Vrogas_Vas "Vrogas Vas"). During a confrontation with Rebel Alliance forces on the planet, Vader found an ancient [Jedi Temple](/wiki/Jedi_Temple_(Vrogas_Vas) "Jedi Temple (Vrogas Vas)"), where he heard disembodied voices of people from his past, including Jinn.[[82]](#cite_note-Vader_Down-82) A few years later, Kenobi appeared as a physical spirit to tell Luke to train with Yoda on Dagobah. He continued to manifest himself to help guide Luke through his training.[[71]](#cite_note-Episode_V-71)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn was considered by Luke Skywalker as a member of the Skywalker family due to his deep connection with the Skywalkers' history with the Jedi.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/15/Luke_Skywalker_Ep_7_SWCT.png/revision/latest?cb=20180731193551) [![Qui-Gon Jinn was considered by Luke Skywalker as a member of the Skywalker family due to his deep connection with the Skywalkers' history with the Jedi.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/15/Luke_Skywalker_Ep_7_SWCT.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20180731193551)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/15/Luke_Skywalker_Ep_7_SWCT.png/revision/latest?cb=20180731193551) 

Qui-Gon Jinn was considered by Luke Skywalker as a member of the Skywalker family due to his deep connection with the Skywalkers' history with the Jedi.

 

It was on Dagobah that Yoda fulfilled the destiny first spoken of by the Force Priestesses,[[59]](#cite_note-Destiny-59) training Luke to become a Jedi Knight.[[71]](#cite_note-Episode_V-71) When Skywalker left his training early to save his friends, Kenobi questioned if the boy was the last hope of the Jedi, hearing Jinn, along with any Jedi whose actions had led to current circumstances, in his voice.[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) Jinn himself later appeared as a vision to Luke in the [Living Sea](/wiki/Living_Sea "Living Sea") of [Gazian](/wiki/Gazian "Gazian"), as the imprint of long-past Jedi Master [Elzar Mann](/wiki/Elzar_Mann "Elzar Mann") imparted wisdom upon Skywalker.[[83]](#cite_note-SW2020-20-83) After Skywalker returned to Dagobah, Yoda died shortly after and passed on into the Force, where he retained his identity. Through the training Yoda gave Luke, the boy confronted and [redeemed](/wiki/Battle_of_Endor "Battle of Endor") his father from the dark side, and Anakin killed Darth Sidious. Through this act and his own death, Anakin helped defeat the Galactic Empire, brought balance to the Force, and was able to return as a spirit as well. By killing Sidious and sacrificing himself, Jinn's strongly-held belief was finally proven right; Anakin Skywalker was the Chosen One.[[64]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-64)

In the [years following](/wiki/New_Republic_Era "New Republic Era") Anakin's redemption and fulfillment of the prophecy, Luke embarked on a quest to rediscover the Jedi Order's forgotten history in hopes to re-establish it. In his search for Jedi knowledge, Luke learned about the life of Jinn, his relationship with Obi-Wan Kenobi, his encounter with the Force Priestesses, and the role he played in his father's training. While Jinn was not related to the Skywalkers by blood, his close connection to the family was noted by Luke in his [book](/wiki/Book "Book") *[The Secrets of the Jedi](/wiki/The_Secrets_of_the_Jedi "The Secrets of the Jedi")*, which chronicled the Jedi Order's history.[[84]](#cite_note-TSotJ-84)

In [35 ABY](/wiki/35_ABY "35 ABY"), during the [Battle of Exegol](/wiki/Battle_of_Exegol "Battle of Exegol"), [Rey](/wiki/Rey_Skywalker "Rey Skywalker") heard Jinn's voice among the voices of many Jedi of the past who aided her with destroying the resurrected Darth Sidious for good. "Every Jedi who ever lived lives in you," he told her, adding that they stood behind her.[[85]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-85)

## Personality and traits[]

### Ideals and spirituality[]

#### A unique Jedi[]

:   "*Do not defy the Council, Master, not again.*"  
    "*I shall do what I must, Obi-Wan.*"
:   ―Obi-Wan Kenobi and Qui-Gon Jinn — ![20?cb=20250116042720](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ee/Quote-audio.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/20?cb=20250116042720) [Link](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2c/IShallDoWhatIMust-TPM.flac/revision/latest?cb=20250407192713)▶️ ([file info](/wiki/File:IShallDoWhatIMust-TPM.flac "File:IShallDoWhatIMust-TPM.flac"))[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

Qui-Gon Jinn was a human male who stood 1.93 [meters](/wiki/Meter "Meter") tall[[5]](#cite_note-SWEQui-GonJinn-5) and had light skin, blue [eyes](/wiki/Eye "Eye"),[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) and long,[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36) brown [hair](/wiki/Hair "Hair"), along with a brown beard. Though he had risen to the rank of Jedi Master, Jinn did not always agree with the structures and rules of the Jedi Order. Jinn was known to prefer following the spirit of the Jedi Code than the letter and was willing to rebuff the Jedi Council.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Where all Jedi knew you could love others as long as you were not possessive, Jinn was less concerned with the dangers of strong connections in comparison to his peers.[[45]](#cite_note-Together_Again_Download-45) While he knew the Force could often present more questions than answers, he nevertheless trusted in it and its guidance.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) As a Padawan,[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) his commitment to the Order was tested[[18]](#cite_note-Ultimate_Star_Wars_new-18) by his romantic relationship on Felucia,[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) but he ended up returning to the Jedi.[[18]](#cite_note-Ultimate_Star_Wars_new-18) While he did keep a Mustafar fire diamond he was gifted on Felucia for twenty years as a prized possession, specifically keeping it in a pouch on his belt to ensure it was with him every day, he would ultimately give up the stone to Pax Maripher and Rahara Wick, reflecting to himself that it was the memories, not physical mementos, that mattered.[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn was different from his fellow Jedi, having his own views on the Force that could conflict with the opinions of his peers.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/72/AoR-QuiGonJinn-B-textless.png/revision/latest?cb=20190626042119) [![Qui-Gon Jinn was different from his fellow Jedi, having his own views on the Force that could conflict with the opinions of his peers.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/72/AoR-QuiGonJinn-B-textless.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20190626042119)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/72/AoR-QuiGonJinn-B-textless.png/revision/latest?cb=20190626042119) 

Qui-Gon Jinn was different from his fellow Jedi, having his own views on the Force that could conflict with the opinions of his peers.

 

While during the Clone Wars other Jedi came to focus on meditation to try to understand the future, Jinn lived in the moment.[[5]](#cite_note-SWEQui-GonJinn-5) He believed that one's focus on the future shouldn't compromise their concentration on the present and believed in trusting one's instincts.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Jinn was more interested in obeying the will of the Force than caring about climbing the ranks of Jedi hierarchy,[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) leading to his lack of care about joining the Council despite his own apprentice, Obi-Wan Kenobi, insisting he could secure a spot.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Jinn further believed that a Jedi needed to interpret the Jedi Code for themself, arguing that otherwise the Code would become a prison.[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11)[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) Although he was unconcerned whenever someone claimed he was a coward, Jinn came to have a distaste for how many people, even people on Coruscant, saw the Jedi as warriors and political servants. Although Yoda simply thought that people who could not use the Force would be confused by those who could, Jinn was faced with a great turmoil due to his concerns as he understood that the Order's actions reflected who they really were.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33)

Instead of focusing on what he had expected out of situations, Jinn decided it was best to focus on what actually was happening.[[19]](#cite_note-Life_Day-19) Jinn took the time to truly look at and understand the people he worked with. In the case of Queen Padmé Amidala, she reflected that he had, at times, looked too deeply into her; Jinn realized that she had swapped places with one of her Handmaidens, making him one of the few people who was ever able to deduce the deception tactic. Keeping it a secret that he knew, he would address his questions to the fake queen, making those around them, like fellow Handmaiden Saché, think he had been fooled. Ultimately, Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi taught Amidala that the Jedi were sentient beings like herself, even if she did not understand their teachings.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

While the Jedi Council would disagree with his assessment, Jinn believed that the Jedi being based on Coruscant was part of the problem with the Order's perception as warriors and political servants; their Coruscant temple enabled them to become and be seen as a force that served the Republic, even possibly making themselves believe it.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) Jinn often entered into debates with Jedi Master Mace Windu, but neither of them enjoyed those disagreements.[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21) Ultimately, Jinn could be described as being like a maverick when compared to his fellow Jedi. Although it was a rare viewpoint, he was not the only "maverick" Jedi during the late Republic Era, as Master [Tu-Anh](/wiki/Tu-Anh "Tu-Anh") was also active in the Order. During the Clone Wars, Kenobi compared the two while overlooking Tu-Anh's body after her death.[[86]](#cite_note-A_Death_on_Utapau-86) Still, such a defiant outlook towards the council was rare in Jinn's time. Had Jinn been alive during the High Republic Era, Kenobi once reasoned, he would likely have become a [Wayseeker](/wiki/Wayseeker "Wayseeker"),[[22]](#cite_note-Padawan_Novel-22) a Jedi who operated without direct council oversight[[87]](#cite_note-Into_the_Dark-87) to follow the will of the Force as they felt it.[[88]](#cite_note-THR_7-88)

Jinn was also considered to be a [Jedi Vanguard](/wiki/Jedi_Vanguard "Jedi Vanguard").[[89]](#cite_note-GoH-89)

#### Respect in prophecies and balance[]

:   "*We must all interpret the Code for ourselves or it ceases to be a living pact and becomes nothing but a prison cell.*"
:   ―Qui-Gon Jinn, on the Jedi Code[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11)

Although the other Jedi of his era thought little of prophecies and argued that looking into the future could be dangerous and uncertain, Jinn respected the prophecies made by the Jedi mystics of old. Even though he had in his younger years, Jinn did not view prophecies to be literal. Nevertheless, he did not take them to be meaningless, and he felt that learning what the ancient mystics believed helped tie the Jedi Order to its history. Still, he did also know that trying to learn the future could be considered a form of control, which could lead to the dark side. Ultimately, he told Obi-Wan Kenobi that explaining his view of the prophecies was "complex."[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn felt that, as a Jedi, he needed to find balance in the Force.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/48/AoR-QuiGonJinn-C-textless.png/revision/latest?cb=20190626042354) [![Qui-Gon Jinn felt that, as a Jedi, he needed to find balance in the Force.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/48/AoR-QuiGonJinn-C-textless.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/217?cb=20190626042354)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/48/AoR-QuiGonJinn-C-textless.png/revision/latest?cb=20190626042354) 

Qui-Gon Jinn felt that, as a Jedi, he needed to find balance in the Force.

 

To Jinn, the ultimate purpose of the Jedi was to find balance. Although he once pondered whether the Force wanted him to learn from the dark side, he came to the conclusion that the dark side's corrupting nature made it so it could never create balance.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) However, much like his argument about the Jedi Code needing to be a living pact instead of a prison cell,[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11) he also believed that, if the Jedi Order acted too rigidly in its beliefs, it too could not achieve balance. Thus, he believed that the Jedi needed to make a compromise between both extremes; they could not bend to the dark side, yet they also could not become too rigid. Jinn used his understanding of balance to help the Priestess of Wood, Th'er, telling her how she could find compromise with people who had faced similar struggles to her, which would allow her to enrich her people while also preserving their culture.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33)

Similarly, Jinn displayed a great respect towards Wookiee culture. He saw that their connection to their homeworld was like a balance, further thinking that their Life Day celebrations were a celebration of the Force. He also respected the wisdom held by members of the Wookiee species, knowing that it could teach both him and his Padawan, Kenobi, many things. His understanding of Wookiee culture also helped in conventional problems; he knew it was odd for any Wookiee to be away from their family on Life Day, helping him to realize something was behind the disappearance of Balfus.[[19]](#cite_note-Life_Day-19) Even after his death and becoming part of the Force, he continued to respect balance and see it as necessary.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Most other Jedi did not seem to share[[90]](#cite_note-Kylo_Ren_4-90) the same concerns as Jinn about how they should act.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) According to [Snoke](/wiki/Snoke "Snoke") during his ongoing seduction of [Ben Solo](/wiki/Ben_Solo "Ben Solo") to the dark side, the Jedi believed their rules made them stronger, and so continued to use a seemingly endless series of rules and codes.[[90]](#cite_note-Kylo_Ren_4-90) Much like how Jinn had compared being too rigid to a tree branch that breaks off in the wind after refusing to accommodate it,[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) Snoke told Solo the rigid nature of the Jedi Order helped to bring about its downfall[[90]](#cite_note-Kylo_Ren_4-90) at the end of the Clone Wars.[[60]](#cite_note-Episode_III-60) Following his death, Jinn knew of how Owen and Beru Lars took in Luke Skywalker despite the risks of raising the boy; he considered them examples of pure heroism, becoming pained and horrified by their deaths.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

#### Beyond the world of the living[]

:   "*You're very nearly corporeal. I've never seen you appear like this.*"  
    "*It is a matter of learning to both claim the physical world and detach one's self from it. A matter of finding center, of calming one's soul and giving one's self over completely to the Force. Some Jedi choose to transition between life and death in that way, though I could scarcely have imagined it when I was alive. Even after death, we continue to learn.*"  
    "*I look forward to learning the art someday. Hopefully in the distant future.*"
:   ―Obi-Wan Kenobi and Qui-Gon Jinn[[91]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice_(short_story)-91)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn existed as part of the Force but retained his sense of self after death](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/90/FACPOV-Gray.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170919195737) [![Qui-Gon Jinn existed as part of the Force but retained his sense of self after death](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/90/FACPOV-Gray.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20170919195737)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/90/FACPOV-Gray.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170919195737) 

Qui-Gon Jinn existed as part of the Force but retained his sense of self after death

 

Even during his life, Jinn understood that the Force was larger than a single Jedi's connection to it, even believing it was larger than the concepts of life and death.[[19]](#cite_note-Life_Day-19) As part of the Living Force after his death,[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) Jinn was able to understand how every aspect of every environment played a part in the [great song of the Whills](/wiki/Great_song_of_the_Whills "Great song of the Whills"); he saw that nothing was barren, as the Force existed within everything, even understanding how the desert of Tatooine was not truly barren, given everything that made it up.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Although his identity had survived death,[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) he no longer had an "individual existence;" no longer existing as "Qui-Gon Jinn" and instead existing as part of the Force, he was unconcerned with linear time, individuality, awareness, and consciousness, even existing beyond what he believed to be the "crude" language used by living humans. Although he thought being part of the Force was a better state, he nevertheless fondly, but distantly, remembered the vitality of his mortal life. He could leave his unity with the Force to commune with the living, yet such an action caused pain, making the definition of himself separate from the Force. Despite providing a vantage point for the complex physical universe, the pain of entering back into individual existence was only endurable to Jinn because he understood he could return to the Force quickly and because he knew he may be needed. He also found that using his old Padawan's name was worth separating from being one with the Force.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Existing as a fracture of the Force, he understood that his past existence was best summarized by his name, given that it was who he was during his temporal life.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) He guided Yoda through Dagobah to learn the secret of eternal consciousness; but, Yoda was interested in knowing if Jinn, existing outside of normal time, could tell him Darth Sidious's true identity. Although Jinn hinted that he knew the truth, he explained he could only guide Yoda towards greater knowledge, not provide him with the answers. Jinn's training to retain his identity after death led him to new philosophies unknown to the Jedi Order at the time. Jinn learned that there were two sides to the Force, a Living Force channeled by the energies of all living beings, and the Cosmic Force into which it fed. It was this symbiotic relationship that allowed the Force to bind the galaxy together and speak to living beings through the midi-chlorians.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

 [![Jinn's spirit initially could only manifest as a voice (Yoda pictured in conversation with Jinn's presence).](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bc/YodaDagobahLight.png/revision/latest?cb=20140825120811) [![Jinn's spirit initially could only manifest as a voice (Yoda pictured in conversation with Jinn's presence).](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bc/YodaDagobahLight.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/285?cb=20140825120811)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/bc/YodaDagobahLight.png/revision/latest?cb=20140825120811) 

Jinn's spirit initially could only manifest as a voice (Yoda pictured in conversation with Jinn's presence).

 

After learning how to manifest himself into the physical universe[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) instead of only existing as a voice,[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) he could draw upon the memories of his life, using them to form into a shape that appeared like how his body had. He could feel everything, from his flesh to his robes, form around him; when he was summoned by Obi-Wan Kenobi after Luke Skywalker ran to see what had become of his aunt and uncle, Jinn found that removing his hood came naturally. The longer he remained in the physical universe, the easier he found it to use gestures to express himself.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Jinn thought that the most beautiful type of mastery was learning to let go, such as how Jedi like himself let go from the mortal universe. Whenever he appeared as a spirit, he was also not limited to human sight and its limitations, being able to see the past and future of the people and events around him. Appearing as a spirit required balance and devotion to the Force, with Jinn explaining he needed to both claim and detach himself from the mortal universe. It took nearly a decade of training to be able to enter such a state. The longer he remained in the mortal realm, the more corporeal he became. He was even able to smell the cremation of the Jawas.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Finding human lives incredibly brief and death an inevitable—but almost a neutral—event, Jinn had come to believe that it was one's journey through the Force that mattered. Believing that truths always eventually came out, he was able to know what living people would call the future, as he no longer existed in linear time. When he appeared on Tatooine to speak with Kenobi, he felt the deaths of nearby Jawas, specifically feeling the memory of their helplessness and fear wash over his consciousness. Finding their deaths meaningless, Jinn was comforted by the sight of C-3PO and R2-D2, knowing it proved time to be a circle; the Force had ensured they were present once more on the desert world, making the beginning of a journey its end as well.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Jinn understood that he could never have understood the process of appearing as a spirit when he was alive. Whenever Jinn intended to return to the Force, his awareness spread out, again allowing him to sense how every aspect of a planet fit together to form the system of life. Upon letting go, he again would release his name and form to become one with[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) the energy field that was[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79) the Force.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

### Apprentice of Dooku[]

:   "*I once knew someone, a teacher, a mentor. Someone who I looked to as my guide in all things. He made a choice—he did something that I couldn't fathom. It created a feeling inside me. A doubt and fear that I never thought I could overcome. I was lost for a good while. Shaken to my core. But over time, that fear and doubt became something else—it became resolve. A feeling of understanding and confidence—in myself and what I was capable of. It would have been normal to resent him. To blame this other person's decisions for whatever errors I made. But that would also have been the easy path, a lazy and passive one. […] I trusted myself. I worked harder. I accepted that one man's mistakes would never carry the weight of my own. I studied the Jedi teachings. I interpreted them as best I could. And I listened and learned. We are all flawed, Lizel. We all make errors of judgment. It's how we recover from them that defines us.*"
:   ―Qui-Gon Jinn talks to Lizel Liit about his thoughts on Dooku after the man left the Jedi Order[[23]](#cite_note-Resolve-23)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn remained a weak point for Count Dooku (pictured) well into the former Jedi's days as a Sith Lord.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3c/CountDookuDeviousStrategist-SWDA.png/revision/latest?cb=20201201062045) [![Qui-Gon Jinn remained a weak point for Count Dooku (pictured) well into the former Jedi's days as a Sith Lord.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3c/CountDookuDeviousStrategist-SWDA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20201201062045)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/3c/CountDookuDeviousStrategist-SWDA.png/revision/latest?cb=20201201062045) 

Qui-Gon Jinn remained a weak point for Count Dooku (pictured) well into the former Jedi's days as a Sith Lord.

 

Dooku was Jinn's master[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) and friend.[[24]](#cite_note-AoR_Dooku-24) Further described by Jinn as a teacher and mentor figure who could guide him through any issue, Jinn was nonetheless shocked by Dooku's decision to leave the Jedi Order, with Dooku's choice also creating fear and doubt inside his former disciple. In that mindset, he found himself lost and made several mistakes. In time, however, those concerns Jinn faced would give way to resolve he described as confidence and understanding. While he suspected resenting Dooku would be a normal reaction, he also decided it was the easy, lazy, and passive path; instead, Jinn turned inward and towards his studies, concluding in the end that everyone made mistakes, yet it was how one decided to respond to those errors that mattered the most. His experience after Dooku's decision and his time healing gave him wisdom he imparted to [Lizel Liit](/wiki/Lizel_Liit "Lizel Liit").[[23]](#cite_note-Resolve-23)

In secret, Dooku fell to the dark side and became the Sith Lord Darth Tyranus,[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) yet Jinn remained a crack in Dooku's armor.[[92]](#cite_note-Brotherhood-92) On Geonosis, Dooku claimed to Kenobi that he wished Jinn were still alive so the late Jedi Master could have helped him with the Confederacy of Independent Systems. Kenobi rejected the idea that Jinn would have joined Dooku. Still, Dooku told Kenobi that Jinn knew about the corruption in the Galactic Senate and might have joined the Separatist cause—especially if he had learned that the Republic was under Darth Sidious's control, although, in truth, the CIS was just as much under Sith control as their rival state.[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) Shortly into the war, Kenobi invoked Jinn's memory in debate with Dooku concerning a [mission to the neutral planet Cato Neimoidia](/wiki/Mission_to_Cato_Neimoidia_(Kenobi_and_Skywalker) "Mission to Cato Neimoidia (Kenobi and Skywalker)"), which created a minor but present shift in the Sith Lord's demeanor. Trying to hide his reaction, Dooku only responded by noting Jinn had been an honorable figure, ultimately agreeing that the CIS would let Kenobi carry out the mission when Kenobi declared that he carried on Jinn's teachings and, thus, could be trusted as well.[[92]](#cite_note-Brotherhood-92)

### Mentor to Obi-Wan Kenobi and empathetic nature[]

#### Training the Jedi Padawan[]

:   "*You've been a good apprentice, Obi-Wan. And you're a much wiser man than I am. I foresee you will become a great Jedi Knight.*"
:   ―Qui-Gon Jinn, to Obi-Wan Kenobi[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

During his service to the Jedi Order, Jinn took on Obi-Wan Kenobi as his Padawan learner. Although they were able to work well together, both had major differences in their view of the Jedi;[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) the by-the-book Kenobi[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) was more willing to obey the orders of the Jedi Council,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) being willing to fill out detailed reports of their missions, while Jinn was willing to hold back on such duties, partly because he knew Kenobi would handle them,[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) and disobey the Council.[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21) Kenobi and Jinn's conflicting natures initially caused friction in their relationship, but both grew close over time.[[17]](#cite_note-Timelines-17) Though he still did not entirely agree with it, Kenobi came to understand it was normal for Jinn to disagree with the Council, viewing his Master's actions as a viable alternative to their orders, as it avoided giving into absolutes. Even so, he always preferred to have advanced warning when they were to go on unapproved missions, at least because it allowed him to pack.[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21)

With a Jedi Master who had a more "relaxed" attitude instead of a rigid reading of the [Jedi Code](/wiki/Jedi_Code "Jedi Code"),[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) Kenobi understood that his lessons were often unconventional, but he did not display annoyance with that,[[19]](#cite_note-Life_Day-19) even if Jinn's attempts at moving him away from a standard Jedi viewpoint—asking Kenobi to embody the spirit of the Jedi Code instead of a literal reading—instead resulted in Kenobi trying even harder to embody the traditional Jedi spirit.[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) Jinn nevertheless defended his unconventional choices, believing that Jedi could not learn new lessons if they only stuck with their specific teachings. Beyond thinking Kenobi was always well learned in his answers to questions, Jinn also truly trusted his Padawan; when he and many Wookiees were captured on Life Day, he trusted in Kenobi to rescue them.[[19]](#cite_note-Life_Day-19) He also felt sustained by Kenobi's strength.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi, master and apprentice](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/JediMasterAndPadawan-TPM.png/revision/latest?cb=20130619193229) [![Qui-Gon Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi, master and apprentice](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/JediMasterAndPadawan-TPM.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20130619193229)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d2/JediMasterAndPadawan-TPM.png/revision/latest?cb=20130619193229) 

Qui-Gon Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi, master and apprentice

 

Jinn also tasked Kenobi with reading political bills with him whenever he got a feeling that something was wrong. While Kenobi was annoyed by how time consuming the process was, he respected that, and was further annoyed by how, his mentor's feelings on such matters were often correct. Beyond Jinn often being correct, the other reason he went along with it was because his only attempt at "mutinying" against such work it did not go over well.[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21) Like most Jedi, Kenobi also did not share his master's fascination with prophecies.[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11) Despite their differences, which could make them argue even when they agreed on matters,[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21) Jinn remained proud of Kenobi's accomplishments, believing his Padawan to be wiser than himself and foreseeing that his apprentice would become an great Jedi Knight. Kenobi was also thankful for his teachings[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) and, even despite his misgivings, would not give up their friendly arguments for anything.[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21)

Beyond being able to sense whenever his apprentice held discontentment,[[21]](#cite_note-Queen's_Peril-21) Qui-Gon Jinn had an empathetic nature and tended to take unfortunate life forms under his protection. It was this tendency and his defiance towards the Jedi Council, which often frustrated and baffled his Padawan. When Jinn saved the Gungan exile Jar Jar Binks, who in turn swore a life-debt to him, his compassionate nature was such that Jinn took the hapless Gungan under his wing, much to Kenobi's dismay. His empathy toward all life forms, including the most pitiful and unfortunate, was Jinn's greatest strength.[[1]](#cite_note-Ultimate-1) Additionally, he remained understanding and patient with Queen Padmé Amidala.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36) During the short time they knew each other,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) he never asked for her to do more than she was willing to, and she was left in nearly overwhelming sadness anytime she thought of the Jedi Master after his death.[[36]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-36)

Kenobi had sleepless nights during his training, partly because he feared Jinn would somehow end up removed from the Jedi Order before his apprenticeship was over. Kenobi had tried to embody a traditional Jedi spirit to keep his master in line with traditional teachings, a reverse of the typical master—apprentice relationship. Despite that,[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) some of Jinn's defiance was passed down to his Padawan, resulting in Kenobi pushing for Anakin to become his apprentice.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

#### Remaining a mentor[]

:   "*Thank you, Qui-Gon. As always, your wisdom sustains me.*"  
    "*As your strength always sustained me.*"
:   ―Obi-Wan and Qui-Gon[[91]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice_(short_story)-91)

Even after his death, Jinn continued to help his former Padawan; he gave him guidance during the Imperial Era, warning him whenever he needed to protect Luke Skywalker.[[62]](#cite_note-Time_of_Death-62) When he was called upon during his former student's exile, he did not only see Kenobi as he existed in old age, seeing every other aspect of the man's past and present at once and believing they all made him who he was. In fact, he completed his training to appear as a ghost for Kenobi, as he wanted him to have company throughout his exile. Finding that saying Kenobi's name made the effort to enter the physical universe worth it, he elected to also say "Ben,"[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) which served as Kenobi's alias.[[79]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-79) He also knew that Kenobi would quickly adopt the persona of a Jedi Knight once more, as soon as danger came, and looked forward to watching Kenobi do so.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Jinn also took to calling him "my Padawan" once more, as he knew Kenobi still had much to learn, as he had learned that death was merely the start of gaining wisdom. Even so, he believed Kenobi already personified the ways of the Jedi, seeing that he had the patience to remain on Tatooine as Luke Skywalker grew up. Although Kenobi did not see himself in a kind light, Jinn also knew Kenobi was special for not giving into the dark side during that time; he was in awe of Kenobi's steadfast devotion to the light, as he remained a Jedi despite losing everyone he loved. Beyond his mentor, Kenobi had lost Anakin, Satine Kryze, Padmé Amidala,[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) Ahsoka Tano, and [Clone Commander](/wiki/Clone_Commander "Clone Commander") [Cody](/wiki/Cody "Cody").[[42]](#cite_note-Ahsoka-42) He also respected Kenobi's courage in wanting to continue to live despite all he had lost; he was moved by this, but he anticipated the upcoming reunion they would have after Kenobi's death.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

He felt that respecting Kenobi's steadfast devotion to the Jedi was something he owed his Padawan because, upon reflection, Jinn also believed he had failed his student, thinking that Kenobi had not been ready to teach Anakin. He thought his mistakes were obvious and wretched, thinking that Kenobi never discussed them with him to spare his mentor needing to hear of them. In reality,[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) even though he did feel Anakin had been thrust upon him and did regret not having more time to figure out his place in the Jedi Order,[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39) Kenobi never mentioned the supposed mistakes to his former master because he did not blame him for Anakin's fall. Jinn wanted to discuss these matters with Kenobi once they were both beyond the world of the living, and he agreed with his apprentice's decision to not tell Luke the full story about his father, thinking that the boy needed to learn when he was steady and strong in the Force.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

Kenobi felt sustained by his mentor's wisdom, looking forward to learning how to appear as a spirit and never hesitating to call upon Jinn. Whenever Jinn departed from the mortal world to return to the Force, he found that Kenobi became another part of the overall music of life. He intended to show Kenobi the beauty in letting go to be a part of the Force.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) By the time after his death, Kenobi had come to disagree with the way Jinn had taken Skywalker off Tatooine; the Jedi Master had told the boy he was not on planet to free him from slavery, instead suggesting he leave his mother for a prophecy he had never heard of.[[39]](#cite_note-There_is_Always_Another-39)

### Belief in Anakin Skywalker[]

:   "*Do you believe you are the Chosen One?*"  
    "*How can I know?*"  
    "*I can tell you what I believe. I believe you will bring balance to the Force. That you will face your demons and save the universe.*"
:   ―Qui-Gon Jinn and Anakin Skywalker — ![20?cb=20250116042720](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ee/Quote-audio.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/20?cb=20250116042720) [Link](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/QuiGonAnakinMortis.flac/revision/latest?cb=20251007211816)▶️ ([file info](/wiki/File:QuiGonAnakinMortis.flac "File:QuiGonAnakinMortis.flac"))[[51]](#cite_note-GhostsMortis-51)

 [![Meeting the young boy Anakin Skywalker, Qui-Gon Jinn was certain he was the Chosen One.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5d/5MinuteStories-Anakin-and-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20210727004301) [![Meeting the young boy Anakin Skywalker, Qui-Gon Jinn was certain he was the Chosen One.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5d/5MinuteStories-Anakin-and-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20210727004301)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5d/5MinuteStories-Anakin-and-Qui-Gon.png/revision/latest?cb=20210727004301) 

Meeting the young boy Anakin Skywalker, Qui-Gon Jinn was certain he was the Chosen One.

 

Unlike Kenobi,[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11) Jinn believed in the prophecy of the Chosen One, being certain that the foretold individual would bring balance to the Force.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Just as the prophecy foretold,[[11]](#cite_note-Master_&_Apprentice-11) Jinn came to meet a male born of no father, Anakin Skywalker, and he quickly came to believe he was the Chosen One. Though he acknowledged that Skywalker's future contained an uncertain destiny, he did not dwell on the danger the Council saw in Skywalker's potential. He was willing to train him even if the council forbade it. Even in his dying deaths, Jinn remained steadfast in his belief.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

Even as a spirit, Jinn continued to believe in Skywalker, quickly asking Kenobi whether he had trained him when they reunited on Mortis.
