Although he briefly entertained the thought that Skywalker was not the Chosen One, warning Kenobi that the planet was nevertheless dangerous for Skywalker even if he was not,[[50]](#cite_note-Overlords-50) he later affirmed his faith in the young Jedi and his destiny while speaking to him.[[51]](#cite_note-GhostsMortis-51) Skywalker and Kenobi later came to believe their discussions with Jinn's spirit on Mortis were deceptions,[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) but it had truly been their old mentor.[[52]](#cite_note-CVD-52)

After Skywalker fell to the dark side, Jinn saw it as a fate worse than death. He blamed himself for the creation of Darth Vader, believing that he had placed the responsibility for training him on Kenobi before his student was ready. He concluded that training the boy may have been impossible for even the best of the Jedi, yet Kenobi disagreed;[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) although Kenobi too had once blamed himself for Skywalker's fall, Vader rebutted that idea during their duel on a barren moon, declaring that he himself had destroyed Skywalker, not his masters.[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63) As such, Kenobi argued to Jinn that Skywalker—even if himself and Jinn had some blame for his fate—had all the wisdom needed to take the path of the light side, yet he chose otherwise. Despite agreeing with Kenobi's response, he did not feel his mistakes were absolved.[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66)

## Powers and abilities[]

:   "*Show yourself, can you?*"  
    "*I cannot. My training was incomplete. All energy from the Living Force, from all things that have ever lived, feeds into the Cosmic Force, binding everything and communicating to us through the midi-chlorians. Because of this, I can speak to you now.*"
:   ―Yoda communes with Jinn on Dagobah about eternal consciousness[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

 [![Qui-Gon Jinn knew the secret to maintaining himself after death](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6f/QuiGonJinn9BBY-OWKp6.png/revision/latest?cb=20250105064713) [![Qui-Gon Jinn knew the secret to maintaining himself after death](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6f/QuiGonJinn9BBY-OWKp6.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20250105064713)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6f/QuiGonJinn9BBY-OWKp6.png/revision/latest?cb=20250105064713) 

Qui-Gon Jinn knew the secret to maintaining himself after death

 

Regarded by his fellows as a great Jedi,[[24]](#cite_note-AoR_Dooku-24) Qui-Gon Jinn was sensitive to and had an affinity for the Force. He utilized [telekinesis](/wiki/Telekinesis "Telekinesis") and [mind tricks](/wiki/Mind_trick "Mind trick") on more than one occasion, using them to help further his goals during the Trade Federation's occupation of Naboo and while attempting to free Skywalker from slavery.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) A testament to his power in the Force was when during his mission on [Planet WG4587](/wiki/Planet_WG4587 "Planet WG4587") he managed to lift and entire [CR70 corvette](/wiki/CR70_corvette "CR70 corvette") through telekinesis.[[93]](#cite_note-Jedi_Knights_3-93) He was also skilled in the ability of Force jump, being able to use it to leap high into the air. While Jinn was disturbed by the concept that he could be seen as a warrior, believing such a title was not what a Jedi was meant to be,[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) Jinn was skilled with a lightsaber. He was able to use his blade to easily defeat battle droids on Naboo and hold his own in his first duel with Darth Maul. During his second duel with Maul, the Sith Lord out-fought the Jedi Master and mortally wounded him after a prolonged fight. Although Jinn fell at the hands of Maul,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) his influence remained present in his former apprentice Kenobi as well as his apprentice, Anakin Skywalker. When Kenobi and Skywalker confronted Dooku on his ship during the Clone Wars, the Sith Lord noted that he had to be wary of their knowledge and skill since they had been taught by Jinn, who at one point had been his Padawan.[[47]](#cite_note-Dooku_Captured_story-47)

The ability to manifest consciousness after death was, for a time, a skill that other Jedi didn't know. Jinn kept his training with the Force Priestesses a secret, and the Jedi Order continued to believe that death was permanent and one couldn't retain their identity. It was not until towards the Clone Wars that Jinn revealed himself to Yoda, despite his training being incomplete at the time, and Jinn told the Jedi Master that he too could learn to return from death through the Cosmic Force.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) In this state, Jinn's connection to the Force was not hampered by a physical body; he was of the Force, so could see possibilities and what was occurring in multiple locations at once. As such, he could sense events before they happened. Jinn passed his teachings[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) on to Yoda and Kenobi, who used it and the new philosophies they learned to help guide Luke Skywalker towards his destiny.[[64]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-64) He also completed his training himself, ensuring he could appear physically[[66]](#cite_note-Master_and_Apprentice-66) instead of just as a voice.[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31)

## Equipment[]

### Tools and clothing[]

 [![A member of the Jedi Order, Qui-Gon Jinn wore traditional Jedi robes.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f2/QuiGonJinn-SWBC67.png/revision/latest?cb=20240220054748) [![A member of the Jedi Order, Qui-Gon Jinn wore traditional Jedi robes.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f2/QuiGonJinn-SWBC67.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20240220054748)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f2/QuiGonJinn-SWBC67.png/revision/latest?cb=20240220054748) 

A member of the Jedi Order, Qui-Gon Jinn wore traditional Jedi robes.

 

Like his fellow Jedi, Qui-Gon Jinn wore the Jedi robes typical of his era, including an optional hooded robe that could easily be removed. During his time on Tatooine, he wore a [poncho](/wiki/Poncho "Poncho"). Jinn also used a [Hush-98 comlink](/wiki/Hush-98_comlink "Hush-98 comlink") for long distance communication and to transmit a blood sample for midi-chlorian analysis, owned an [imagecaster](/wiki/Imagecaster "Imagecaster") to display holograms, and used an [A99 aquata](/wiki/A99_aquata_breather "A99 aquata breather") [rebreather](/wiki/Rebreather "Rebreather") when swimming underwater.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

Jinn flew a blue Delta-7 *Aethersprite*-class light interceptor, which could be attached to a [hyperspace transport ring](/wiki/Hyperspace_transport_ring "Hyperspace transport ring") for [lightspeed](/wiki/Lightspeed "Lightspeed") travel. Furthermore, his starfighter travels were aided by an astromech droid that had a round dome. For their mission to Bri'n, Kenobi and Jinn used a *Eta*-class shuttle.[[33]](#cite_note-AoR-Q-GJ1-33) During the Invasion of Naboo, Kenobi, Jar Jar Binks, and him were given a Gungan bongo submarine to travel through Naboo's planet core.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

### Lightsaber[]

 [![Jinn was skilled with a lightsaber, but disliked being considered a warrior.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/27/QuiGonJinn-TLC.png/revision/latest?cb=20230613014837) [![Jinn was skilled with a lightsaber, but disliked being considered a warrior.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/27/QuiGonJinn-TLC.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20230613014837)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/27/QuiGonJinn-TLC.png/revision/latest?cb=20230613014837) 

Jinn was skilled with a lightsaber, but disliked being considered a warrior.

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Qui-Gon Jinn's lightsaber](/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn%27s_lightsaber "Qui-Gon Jinn's lightsaber")

The Jedi Master wielded a green lightsaber, that he carried throughout most of his life. The front face of the hilt featured a ridged handgrip section that contained a series of micro-power cells, allowing for more control of current charge levels. The lightsaber had a red button that served as an activation switch. With a hilt length of 28.5 [centimeters](/wiki/Centimeter "Centimeter") and a width of 3.8 centimeters, and made of alloy metal, Jinn's lightsaber was less ornate than the lightsaber belonging to his master, Dooku.[[94]](#cite_note-AGTWOTF-94) Following his death,[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) Jinn's lightsaber fell into the possession of Kenobi,[[65]](#cite_note-Jedi_in_Hiding-65) his apprentice.[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7)

## Behind the scenes[]

:   "*He's almost like a monk, an old-time warrior who is wise and quite philosophical, yet very skilled in martial arts. He has incredible confidence, as well as a magical quality that enables him to see into the future. He's not really a rebel, but he has his own code.*"
:   ―Liam Neeson's thoughts on his character, Qui-Gon Jinn[[95]](#cite_note-TPM_Making_of-95)

 [![Concept art of Qui-Gon Jinn](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6a/Qui-Gon_Jinn_Concept_Art.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090612045122) [![Concept art of Qui-Gon Jinn](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6a/Qui-Gon_Jinn_Concept_Art.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/173?cb=20090612045122)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6a/Qui-Gon_Jinn_Concept_Art.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090612045122) 

Concept art of Qui-Gon Jinn

 

Qui-Gon Jinn was portrayed by [Liam Neeson](/wiki/Liam_Neeson "Liam Neeson") in the [1999](/wiki/1999 "1999") [prequel trilogy](/wiki/Prequel_trilogy "Prequel trilogy") film, [*Star Wars*: Episode I *The Phantom Menace*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_I_The_Phantom_Menace "Star Wars: Episode I The Phantom Menace").[[7]](#cite_note-Episode_I-7) The actor reprised his role in three episodes of *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*; "[Overlords](/wiki/Overlords "Overlords"),"[[50]](#cite_note-Overlords-50) "[Ghosts of Mortis](/wiki/Ghosts_of_Mortis "Ghosts of Mortis"),"[[51]](#cite_note-GhostsMortis-51) and "[Voices](/wiki/Voices "Voices")."[[31]](#cite_note-Voices-31) Audio of him could briefly be heard in [*Star Wars*: Episode II *Attack of the Clones*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_Attack_of_the_Clones "Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones").[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_II-12) Neeson was also set to lend his voice to [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), and Neeson had hinted at his involvement in early [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005").[[96]](#cite_note-USA-96) The scene ultimately appeared in the film's [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Revenge_of_the_Sith_(novelization) "Star Wars: Revenge of the Sith (novelization)").[[97]](#cite_note-Episode_III_novel-97)

Neeson reprised his role again in [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019") in a brief audio cameo in [*Star Wars*: Episode IX *The Rise of Skywalker*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IX_The_Rise_of_Skywalker "Star Wars: Episode IX The Rise of Skywalker"), the final film of the [Skywalker saga](/wiki/Star_Wars_saga "Star Wars saga").[[85]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-85) He once again reprised the role in [2022](/wiki/2022 "2022") in "[Part VI](/wiki/Part_VI "Part VI")" of the series [*Star Wars:* *Obi-Wan Kenobi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi") as a Force ghost.[[63]](#cite_note-Part_VI-63) He spoke to director [Deborah Chow](/wiki/Deborah_Chow "Deborah Chow") and she told him that [Ewan McGregor](/wiki/Ewan_McGregor "Ewan McGregor") would reprise his role as Obi-Wan Kenobi in a series. She explained that when Kenobi was going through a journey, he reached out for help but Jinn was not there. Kenobi would finally see Jinn at the end of his journey. Neeson then said he was definitely onboard with the series.[[98]](#cite_note-Return-98) Neeson returned to the role once more lending his voice to the animated [*Star Wars: Tales of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Tales_of_the_Jedi_(television_series) "Star Wars: Tales of the Jedi (television series)"), while a younger Jinn was voiced by Neeson's son, [Micheál Richardson](/wiki/Miche%C3%A1l_Richardson "Micheál Richardson"). In [2024](/wiki/2024 "2024"), Neeson said he was too old to return to Qui-Gon Jinn in a live-action capacity.[[99]](#cite_note-Interview_2024-99)

Compared to the final screenplay, early drafts of *The Phantom Menace* did not have Qui-Gon Jinn joining Obi-Wan Kenobi until much later in the film, leaving Kenobi as the sole Jedi participant through many of the film's early events, such as the failed negotiations aboard the Trade Federation flagship. Additionally, the final screenplay described Qui-Gon Jinn as being in his 60s, far older than actor Liam Neeson was at the time.[[100]](#cite_note-old-db-jinn-100)

[↑](#cite_ref-The_Lesson_OW_25-0) *"[The Lesson (Obi-Wan & Anakin)](/wiki/The_Lesson_(Obi-Wan_%26_Anakin) "The Lesson (Obi-Wan & Anakin)")" — [*Star Wars* (2020) 25](/wiki/Star_Wars_(2020)_25 "Star Wars (2020) 25")* 26. ↑ [26.0](#cite_ref-Voyage_of_Temptation_26-0) [26.1](#cite_ref-Voyage_of_Temptation_26-1) [26.2](#cite_ref-Voyage_of_Temptation_26-2) [26.3](#cite_ref-Voyage_of_Temptation_26-3) [TCW mini logo](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars") *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* — "[Voyage of Temptation](/wiki/Voyage_of_Temptation "Voyage of Temptation")" 27. [↑](#cite_ref-41-39_Date_Note_27-0) According to [*The Official Star Wars Fact File Part* 98](/wiki/The_Official_Star_Wars_Fact_File_Part_98 "The Official Star Wars Fact File Part 98") MAN 1-4: Mandalore, the [Mandalorian](/wiki/Mandalorian "Mandalorian") Civil War took place around 20 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the [Clone Wars](/wiki/Clone_Wars "Clone Wars"). *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")* establishes that the [Clone](/wiki/Cloning "Cloning") Wars took place starting in [22 BBY](/wiki/22_BBY "22 BBY") through [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"). Therefore, the Mandalorian Civil War can be dated to around [42 BBY](/wiki/42_BBY "42 BBY") to [39 BBY](/wiki/39_BBY "39 BBY"). By the [time](/wiki/Time "Time") of [*Padawan*](/wiki/Padawan_(novel) "Padawan (novel)"), which *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates the events of to [41 BBY](/wiki/41_BBY "41 BBY"), author [Kiersten White](/wiki/Kiersten_White "Kiersten White") establishes that the novel's plot was [explicitly written](https://web.archive.org/web/20220226214721/https://dorksideoftheforce.com/2022/02/26/kiersten-white-talks-star-wars-padawan/) to convey that he had not met [Satine Kryze](/wiki/Satine_Kryze "Satine Kryze"). As [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi") is established to have met Kryze during the Mandalorian Civil War in [TCW mini logo](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars") *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* — "[Voyage of Temptation](/wiki/Voyage_of_Temptation "Voyage of Temptation")", the war must have taken place between around [41 BBY](/wiki/41_BBY "41 BBY") and [39 BBY](/wiki/39_BBY "39 BBY"). 28. [↑](#cite_ref-Fact_File_28-0) [*The Official Star Wars Fact File Part* 98](/wiki/The_Official_Star_Wars_Fact_File_Part_98 "The Official Star Wars Fact File Part 98") MAN 1-4: Mandalore 29. [↑](#cite_ref-Part_I_67-0) [Obi-Wan Kenobi new series logo](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi") *[Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi")* — "[Part I](/wiki/Part_I "Part I")" 68. ↑ [68.0](#cite_ref-Time_of_Death_flashback_date_68-0) [68.1](#cite_ref-Time_of_Death_flashback_date_68-1) "[Time of Death](/wiki/Time_of_Death "Time of Death")" — *[From a Certain Point of View](/wiki/From_a_Certain_Point_of_View "From a Certain Point of View")* establishes that [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker") was three [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") old during a bandit attack on the [Lars Homestead](/wiki/Lars_homestead "Lars homestead"). As he was born in [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), which is dated to [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY") by *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")*, the attack must have been in [16 BBY](/wiki/16_BBY "16 BBY"). 69. [↑](#cite_ref-SurvivorDate_69-0) [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") [Star Wars Jedi: Survivor](https://www.starwars.com/games-apps/star-wars-jedi-survivor) on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20220527232840/https://www.starwars.com/games-apps/star-wars-jedi-survivor)) dates *[Star Wars Jedi: Survivor](/wiki/Star_Wars_Jedi:_Survivor "Star Wars Jedi: Survivor")* to five [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the events of *[Star Wars Jedi: Fallen Order](/wiki/Star_Wars_Jedi:_Fallen_Order "Star Wars Jedi: Fallen Order")*, which equates to [9 BBY](/wiki/9_BBY "9 BBY") per *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")*. 70. [↑](#cite_ref-Kenobi_VI_date_70-0) *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates the events of *[Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi")* to [9 BBY](/wiki/9_BBY "9 BBY"). Therefore, the events of "[Part VI](/wiki/Part_VI "Part VI")" must be set in 9 [BBY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system"). 71. ↑ [71.0](#cite_ref-Episode_V_71-0) [71.1](#cite_ref-Episode_V_71-1) [71.2](#cite_ref-Episode_V_71-2) [*Star Wars*: Episode V *The Empire Strikes Back*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_V_The_Empire_Strikes_Back "Star Wars: Episode V The Empire Strikes Back") 72. [↑](#cite_ref-Twin_Suns_date_75-0) According to *[Star Wars: Absolutely Everything You Need to Know, Updated and Expanded](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Absolutely_Everything_You_Need_to_Know,_Updated_and_Expanded "Star Wars: Absolutely Everything You Need to Know, Updated and Expanded")*, [Maul](/wiki/Maul "Maul")'s final confrontation with [Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Obi-Wan Kenobi") in "[Twin Suns](/wiki/Twin_Suns_(episode) "Twin Suns (episode)")" happened thirty years after Kenobi first saw him on [Tatooine](/wiki/Tatooine "Tatooine"). Since *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")* dates that event to [32 BBY](/wiki/32_BBY "32 BBY"), Kenobi and Maul's final confrontation happened in [2 BBY](/wiki/2_BBY "2 BBY"). 76.
